## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The relationship encodes restoring forces, damping, and potential driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Full Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (Duffing + damping + driving)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (nonlinear pendulum restoring force)
- Damped pendulum driven: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven damped pendulum)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + c3 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinearity / asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Mathieu-like parametric: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) (parametric excitation)
- Cubic-quintic Duffing driven: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (general driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (combined quadratic and cubic restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x^3, x^5) indicate symmetric potential wells; even powers (x^2) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Products of v with powers of x (e.g., v*x^2) indicate amplitude-dependent or position-dependent damping (van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal functions of time (sin(c*t), cos(c*t)) indicate external periodic driving forces
- Sinusoidal functions of position (sin(c*x)) indicate periodic potential landscapes like pendulum dynamics
- Parametric terms like x*cos(c*t) indicate time-modulated stiffness (parametric resonance)
- If acceleration depends only on x and v (not t), the system is autonomous and phase-plane analysis applies
- Negative coefficient on odd-power x terms with positive coefficient on lower-order terms suggests double-well potential (bistability)

**GT:** `-0.0230405406738805*v**3 - 1.1056075693807*x*(0.0552411020531317*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 1.1056075693807*x + 0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

Simplifying the GT:
- `-0.0230405*v³` (nonlinear in v, specifically v³)
- `-1.10561*x*(0.05524*|v|^(1/3) + 1) - 1.10561*x` = `-1.10561*x*0.05524*|v|^(1/3) - 1.10561*x - 1.10561*x` = `-0.06111*x*|v|^(1/3) - 2.21122*x`
- `0.35078*sin(t)`

So GT = `-0.0230405*v³ - 0.06111*x*|v|^(1/3) - 2.21122*x + 0.35078*sin(t)`

Key features of the GT:
1. **v³ term** - cubic in v
2. **x·|v|^(1/3) term** - product of x and fractional power of |v|
3. **Linear x term**
4. **sin(t) term**

Now I need to check if any candidate can reproduce these nonlinear terms.

Most candidates are **linear** in v and x (with various t-dependent coefficients), combined with cos terms in t. These cannot produce v³ or x·|v|^(1/3) terms.

Let me check the special candidates:

**Candidate 1:** `c0*x + c1*x³ + c2*v + c3*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*x²` - Has x³ and x² but no v³ or x·|v|^(1/3). No match.

**Candidate 41:** `c0*v/(c1*t+c2) + c3*v^c4 + c5*cos(c6*t)/(c1*t+c2) + c7*t*v/(c1*t+c2) + c8*t*cos(c6*t)/(c1*t+c2) + c9*x/(c1*t+c2)` - Has v^c4 which could be v³ (set c4=3). But the x term is x/(c1*t+c2), which is t-dependent unless c1=0. If c1=0, then terms become v/c2, v³, cos(c6*t)/c2, t*v/c2, t*cos(c6*t)/c2, x/c2. The sin(t) in GT would need cos(c6*t) terms to produce sin(t), but cos can't become sin. Also, there's t*v and t*cos terms that can't be eliminated (setting coefficients to 0 removes them). With c7=0 and c8=0, we get: c0*v/c2 + c3*v³ + c5*cos(c6*t)/c2 + c9*x/c2. This gives linear v, v³, cos, and x terms. But GT has sin(t), not cos. cos(c6*t) ≠ sin(t) for all t. No match.

**Candidate 29:** Has log(c6*x+1) - can approximate x for small x but isn't equivalent. No match.

**Candidate 43:** Has log(c6*v+1) - similarly can't match v³. No match.

All other candidates are essentially linear combinations of v, x, cos, and t-dependent rational functions of these. None can produce v³ or x·|v|^(1/3).

The only candidate with a nonlinear v term is **Candidate 41** with v^c4, but it uses cos instead of sin and has the x·|v|^(1/3) cross-term missing. Even if we could handle cos vs sin (we can't - cos(t-π/2) = sin(t) but the argument structure doesn't allow phase shifts), the x·|v|^(1/3) term is absent from all candidates.

No candidate can reproduce the `x·|v|^(1/3)` cross-term that appears in the GT, making an exact match impossible.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

I need to analyze whether any candidate can match the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0230405406738805*v**3 - 1.1056075693807*x*(0.0552411020531317*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 1.1056075693807*x + 0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

Expanding:
`-0.0230405406738805*v**3 - 0.0610788368*|v|^(1/3)*x - 1.1056075693807*x - 1.1056075693807*x + 0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

= `-0.0230405406738805*v**3 - 0.0610788368*|v|^(1/3)*x - 2.2112151387614*x + 0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

The GT contains these basis functions:
1. `v**3` (cubic in v)
2. `|v|^(1/3) * x` (product of cube root of |v| and x)
3. `x` (linear in x)
4. `sin(t)` (sine of t)

Key observations:
- The GT has `v**3` — a cubic power of v
- The GT has `|v|^(1/3) * x` — an absolute value with fractional power times x
- The GT has `sin(t)` — which equals `cos(t - π/2)`

Now let me check each candidate:

**Most candidates** contain terms like `v/(c1*t + c2)`, `t*v/(c1*t+c2)`, `cos(ct)`, `x/(c1*t+c2)`, `t*x/(c1*t+c2)`, etc. These are all **rational functions of t** multiplied by v or x, plus cosine terms. None of these can produce `v**3` or `|v|^(1/3)*x`.

Let me check specific candidates that might have nonlinear v terms:

**Candidate 1:** `c0*x + c1*x**3 + c2*v + c3*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*x**2`
Has `x**3`, `x**2`, `x`, `v`, `sin(t)`. Missing `v**3` and `|v|^(1/3)*x`. Cannot match.

**Candidate 29:** Contains `log(c6*x + 1)` — logarithmic, not matching.

**Candidate 41:** `c0*v/(c1*t+c2) + c3*v**c4 + ...`
Has `v**c4` which could be `v**3` if c4=3. But still needs `|v|^(1/3)*x` which isn't present. The x terms are `c9*x/(c1*t+c2)` — rational in t, not matching the constant coefficient needed. Also missing the `|v|^(1/3)*x` cross term.

**Candidate 43:** Contains `log(c6*v + 1)` — logarithmic, not matching.

For all the rational-in-t candidates (most of them): Setting `c1=0` in denominators like `c1*t + c2` makes them constant, giving linear combinations of `v`, `x`, `cos(ct)`, `t*v`, `t*cos(ct)`, `t*x`, etc. None can produce `v**3` or `|v|^(1/3)*x`.

After careful analysis, **no candidate** contains the necessary `v**3` term AND `|v|^(1/3)*x` cross-term that appear in the GT.
